 1952: 
 1953: =head2 sending_software()
 1954: 
 1955: Returns information extracted from headers that identify the software or
 1956: server-side infrastructure used to compose or inject the message.  These
 1957: headers are injected by email clients, bulk-mailing libraries, and shared
 1958: hosting control panels, and are often the most direct evidence of how the
 1959: spam was sent and from which server.
 1960: 
 1961: Headers examined: C<X-Mailer>, C<User-Agent>, C<X-PHP-Originating-Script>,
 1962: C<X-Source>, C<X-Source-Args>, C<X-Source-Host>.
 1963: 
 1964: The C<X-PHP-Originating-Script>, C<X-Source>, and C<X-Source-Host> headers
 1965: in particular are injected automatically by many shared hosting providers
 1966: (cPanel, Plesk, DirectAdmin) and reveal the exact PHP script path and
 1967: hostname responsible.  A hosting abuse team can use these values to
 1968: identify the compromised or malicious account immediately, without needing
 1969: to search logs.
 1970: 
 1971: The data is extracted synchronously during C<parse_email()> with no network
 1972: I/O.  This method simply returns the pre-built list.
 1973: 
 1974: =head3 Usage
 1975: 
 1976:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 1977:     my @sw = $analyser->sending_software();
 1978: 
 1979:     for my $s (@sw) {
 1980:         printf "%-30s : %s\n", $s->{header}, $s->{value};
 1981:         printf "  Note: %s\n", $s->{note};
 1982:     }
 1983: 
 1984:     # Check for shared-hosting injection headers
 1985:     my @hosting = grep {
 1986:         $_->{header} =~ /^x-(?:php-originating-script|source)/
 1987:     } @sw;
 1988: 
 1989:     if (@hosting) {
 1990:         print "Shared-hosting script detected -- report to hosting abuse team:\n";
 1991:         print "  $_->{header}: $_->{value}\n" for @hosting;
 1992:     }
 1993: 
 1994:     # Extract the mailer name if present
 1995:     my ($mailer) = grep { $_->{header} eq 'x-mailer' } @sw;
 1996:     printf "Sent with: %s\n", $mailer->{value} if $mailer;
 1997: 
 1998: =head3 Arguments
 1999: 
 2000: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 2001: 
 2002: =head3 Returns
 2003: 
 2004: A list (not an arrayref) of hashrefs, one per recognised software-fingerprint
 2005: header that was present in the message, in alphabetical order of header name.
 2006: Returns an empty list if none of the watched headers are present, or if
 2007: C<parse_email()> has not been called.
 2008: 
 2009:     {
 2010:         header => 'X-PHP-Originating-Script',
 2011:         value  => '1000:newsletter.php',
 2012:         note   => 'PHP script on shared hosting - report to hosting abuse team',
 2013:     }
 2014: 
 2015: Each hashref contains exactly three keys, all always present:
 2016: 
 2017: =over 4
 2018: 
 2019: =item C<header> (string)
 2020: 
 2021: The header name, lower-cased.  One of the six values listed in the
 2022: Algorithm section below.
 2023: 
 2024: =item C<value> (string)
 2025: 
 2026: The header value exactly as it appeared in the message (not decoded or
 2027: transformed in any way).
 2028: 
 2029: =item C<note> (string)
 2030: 
 2031: A fixed, human-readable annotation describing what this header represents
 2032: and the recommended action.  The note string is determined by the header
 2033: name and is the same for all messages; it is not derived from the value.
 2034: See the Algorithm section for the note associated with each header.
 2035: 
 2036: =back
 2037: 
 2038: =head3 Side Effects
 2039: 
 2040: None.  All data is collected during C<parse_email()> and this method
 2041: only returns the pre-collected list.  No network I/O is performed.
 2042: 
 2043: =head3 Algorithm: headers examined
 2044: 
 2045: The following six headers are examined during C<parse_email()>.  They are
 2046: checked in alphabetical order; the result list preserves that order
 2047: (i.e. C<user-agent> appears before C<x-mailer> which appears before
 2048: C<x-php-originating-script>, etc.).  At most one entry per header name is
 2049: produced even if the header appears more than once; the first occurrence is
 2050: used.
 2051: 
 2052: =over 4
 2053: 
 2054: =item C<user-agent>
 2055: 
 2056: Note: C<"Email client identifier">
 2057: 
 2058: Set by some email clients (Thunderbird, Evolution) as an alternative to
 2059: C<X-Mailer>.  Identifies the application that composed the message.
 2060: 
 2061: =item C<x-mailer>
 2062: 
 2063: Note: C<"Email client or bulk-mailer identifier">
 2064: 
 2065: The most widely used header for identifying the sending application.
 2066: Values range from standard clients (C<"Apple Mail">, C<"Microsoft Outlook">)
 2067: to bulk-mailing libraries (C<"PHPMailer 6.0">, C<"MailMate">).  Its presence
 2068: in spam often reveals the library used to generate the campaign.
 2069: 
 2070: =item C<x-php-originating-script>
 2071: 
 2072: Note: C<"PHP script on shared hosting -- report to hosting abuse team">
 2073: 
 2074: Injected by cPanel and similar shared-hosting control panels when a PHP
 2075: script sends mail via the local MTA.  The value typically takes the form
 2076: C<uid:script.php> (e.g. C<"1000:newsletter.php">), directly identifying
 2077: the Unix user account and the script responsible.  This is the single most
 2078: actionable header for shared-hosting abuse reports.
 2079: 
 2080: =item C<x-source>
 2081: 
 2082: Note: C<"Source file on shared hosting -- report to hosting abuse team">
 2083: 
 2084: Also injected by shared-hosting platforms, typically containing the full
 2085: filesystem path to the sending script (e.g.
 2086: C<"/home/user/public_html/contact.php">).  Complements
 2087: C<X-PHP-Originating-Script>.
 2088: 
 2089: =item C<x-source-args>
 2090: 
 2091: Note: C<"Command-line args injected by shared hosting provider">
 2092: 
 2093: The command-line arguments of the process that sent the mail, injected by
 2094: some hosting platforms.  May reveal interpreter invocations or script
 2095: parameters useful for forensic analysis.
 2096: 
 2097: =item C<x-source-host>
 2098: 
 2099: Note: C<"Sending hostname injected by shared hosting provider">
 2100: 
 2101: The hostname of the server that submitted the message, injected by the
 2102: hosting platform.  Useful when the IP in the C<Received:> chain is a shared
 2103: outbound relay rather than the originating server.
 2104: 
 2105: =back
 2106: 
 2107: =head3 Notes
 2108: 
 2109: =over 4
 2110: 
 2111: =item *
 2112: 
 2113: The result list is reset to empty by each call to C<parse_email()>.  If no
 2114: watched headers are present in the current message, the list is empty.
 2115: 
 2116: =item *
 2117: 
 2118: The alphabetical ordering of entries is a side effect of iterating over
 2119: the C<%sw_notes> hash in sorted key order.  It is stable across calls on
 2120: the same message.
 2121: 
 2122: =item *
 2123: 
 2124: Header names are stored lower-cased (e.g. C<'x-mailer'>, not C<'X-Mailer'>).
 2125: Header values are stored verbatim, preserving the original case and
 2126: whitespace.
 2127: 
 2128: =item *
 2129: 
 2130: The C<note> field is a fixed annotation string chosen by the module, not
 2131: text extracted from the message.  It is safe to display directly in reports
 2132: without sanitisation.
 2133: 
 2134: =item *
 2135: 
 2136: If both C<X-PHP-Originating-Script> and C<X-Source> are present (common on
 2137: cPanel systems), both are returned as separate list entries.  A caller
 2138: building a hosting abuse report should include all entries whose C<header>
 2139: begins with C<x->.
 2140: 
 2141: =back
 2142: 
 2143: =head3 API Specification
 2144: 
 2145: =head4 Input
 2146: 
 2147:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 2148:     # No arguments.
 2149:     []
 2150: 
 2151: =head4 Output
 2152: 
 2153:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 2154: 
 2155:     # A list (possibly empty) of hashrefs, in alphabetical header-name order:
 2156:     (
 2157:         {
 2158:             type => HASHREF,
 2159:             keys => {
 2160:                 header => {
 2161:                     type  => SCALAR,
 2162:                     regex => qr/^(?:user-agent|x-mailer|x-php-originating-script
 2163:                                    |x-source|x-source-args|x-source-host)$/x,
 2164:                 },
 2165:                 value => {
 2166:                     type => SCALAR,
 2167:                     # Verbatim header value; may be any non-empty string.
 2168:                 },
 2169:                 note => {
 2170:                     type  => SCALAR,
 2171:                     # Fixed annotation string; one of the six strings
 2172:                     # documented in the Algorithm section above.
 2173:                 },
 2174:             },
 2175:         },
 2176:         # ... one hashref per recognised header present, alphabetical order
 2177:     )
 2178: 
 2179:     # Empty list when none of the six watched headers are present.
 2180: 
 2181: =cut
 2182: 
 2183: sub sending_software {
 2184: 	my $self = $_[0];
 2185: 
 2186: 	return @{ $self->{_sending_sw} };
 2187: }
 2188: 
 2189: 
 2190: =head2 received_trail()
 2191: 
 2192: Returns the per-hop tracking data extracted from the C<Received:> header
 2193: chain: the IP address, envelope recipient address, and server-assigned
 2194: session ID for each relay that handled the message.
 2195: 
 2196: When filing an abuse report with a transit ISP or relay operator, these
 2197: are the identifiers their postmaster team needs to look up the specific
 2198: SMTP session in their mail logs.  Without the session ID or envelope
 2199: recipient, an ISP typically cannot locate a single message among billions
 2200: of log entries; with them, the lookup takes seconds.
 2201: 
 2202: The data is extracted synchronously during C<parse_email()> with no network
 2203: I/O.  This method simply returns the pre-built list.
 2204: 
 2205: =head3 Usage
 2206: 
 2207:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 2208:     my @trail = $analyser->received_trail();
 2209: 
 2210:     for my $hop (@trail) {
 2211:         printf "Hop IP : %s\n",  $hop->{ip}       // '(unknown)';
 2212:         printf "  For  : %s\n",  $hop->{for}       if defined $hop->{for};
 2213:         printf "  ID   : %s\n",  $hop->{id}        if defined $hop->{id};
 2214:         printf "  Raw  : %s\n",  $hop->{received};
 2215:         print  "\n";
 2216:     }
 2217: 
 2218:     # Build a list of session IDs to include in an abuse report
 2219:     my @ids = map  { "$_->{ip}: id $_->{id}" }
 2220:               grep { defined $_->{id} }
 2221:               @trail;
 2222: 
 2223:     # Find which ISP handled a particular relay IP
 2224:     my ($hop) = grep { ($_->{ip} // '') eq '91.198.174.5' } @trail;
 2225:     if ($hop) {
 2226:         print "Session ID at that relay: $hop->{id}\n" if defined $hop->{id};
 2227:     }
 2228: 
 2229: =head3 Arguments
 2230: 
 2231: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 2232: 
 2233: =head3 Returns
 2234: 
 2235: A list (not an arrayref) of hashrefs, one per C<Received:> hop from which
 2236: at least one of an IP address, an envelope recipient address, or a server
 2237: session ID could be extracted, in oldest-first order (i.e. the first element
 2238: is the outermost relay, the last element is the most recent hop before your
 2239: own server).  Returns an empty list if no C<Received:> headers are present
 2240: or none yielded any extractable data, or if C<parse_email()> has not been
 2241: called.
 2242: 
 2243:     (
 2244:       { received => '...raw header...', ip => '1.2.3.4',
 2245:         for => 'victim@example.com', id => 'ABC123' },
 2246:       ...
 2247:     )
 2248: 
 2249: Each hashref contains exactly four keys:
 2250: 
 2251: =over 4
 2252: 
 2253: =item C<received> (string, always present)
 2254: 
 2255: The complete raw value of the C<Received:> header for this hop, exactly as
 2256: it appeared in the message.  Suitable for including verbatim in an abuse
 2257: report so the receiving ISP can see the full context.
 2258: 
 2259: =item C<ip> (string or undef)
 2260: 
 2261: The IPv4 address extracted from this C<Received:> hop, or C<undef> if no
 2262: recognisable IPv4 address was found.  Uses the same four-pattern extraction
 2263: priority as C<originating_ip()>: bracketed C<[1.2.3.4]> first, then
 2264: parenthesised, then C<from hostname addr>, then any bare dotted-quad as a
 2265: last resort.  Private, reserved, and trusted IPs are B<not> filtered here;
 2266: all IPs including RFC 1918 addresses are returned as found.  (Filtering is
 2267: applied only by C<originating_ip()>.)
 2268: 
 2269: =item C<for> (string or undef)
 2270: 
 2271: The envelope recipient address extracted from the C<for> clause of the
 2272: C<Received:> header (e.g. C<for E<lt>victim@example.comE<gt>>), or C<undef>
 2273: if no such clause is present or it does not contain a fully-qualified email
 2274: address (one with both a local part and a domain containing at least one
 2275: dot).  Bare postmaster addresses, C<for multiple recipients>, and similar
 2276: non-address forms are not captured and result in C<undef>.
 2277: 
 2278: =item C<id> (string or undef)
 2279: 
 2280: The server's internal session or queue identifier from the C<id> clause
 2281: of the C<Received:> header (e.g. C<with ESMTP id ABC123XYZ>), or C<undef>
 2282: if no C<id> clause is present.  The value is a single whitespace-delimited
 2283: token of word characters and dots; longer or more structured ID formats may
 2284: be truncated at the first whitespace boundary.
 2285: 
 2286: =back
 2287: 
 2288: =head3 Side Effects
 2289: 
 2290: None.  All data is collected during C<parse_email()> and this method only
 2291: returns the pre-collected list.  No network I/O is performed.
 2292: 
 2293: =head3 Algorithm: extraction and ordering
 2294: 
 2295: During C<parse_email()>, the C<Received:> headers are walked in reverse
 2296: message order (i.e. oldest hop first, which is the same order as
 2297: C<originating_ip()>'s chain walk).  For each header:
 2298: 
 2299: =over 4
 2300: 
 2301: =item 1.
 2302: 
 2303: The IP address is extracted using the same four-pattern priority sequence
 2304: documented in C<originating_ip()>.
 2305: 
 2306: =item 2.
 2307: 
 2308: The envelope recipient is extracted with the pattern
 2309: C<\bfor\s+E<lt>?([^\s>]+@[\w.-]+\.[\w]+)E<gt>?> (case-insensitive).  The
 2310: domain portion of the address must contain at least one dot; single-label
 2311: names such as C<postmaster> are not matched.
 2312: 
 2313: =item 3.
 2314: 
 2315: The session ID is extracted with the pattern C<\bid\s+([\w.-]+)>
 2316: (case-insensitive), capturing the first word-character token following the
 2317: keyword C<id>.
 2318: 
 2319: =item 4.
 2320: 
 2321: If none of the three fields can be extracted (all are C<undef>), the hop is
 2322: silently discarded and does not appear in the result list.  This suppresses
 2323: internal or synthetic hops that carry no useful tracking information.
 2324: 
 2325: =back
 2326: 
 2327: The result list therefore contains only hops that carry at least one
 2328: actionable piece of tracking data.
 2329: 
 2330: =head3 Notes
 2331: 
 2332: =over 4
 2333: 
 2334: =item *
 2335: 
 2336: The result list is reset to empty by each call to C<parse_email()>.  It
 2337: reflects the C<Received:> headers of the current message only.
 2338: 
 2339: =item *
 2340: 
 2341: Oldest-first ordering means C<$trail[0]> is the first relay the message
 2342: passed through after leaving the sender, and C<$trail[-1]> is the last hop
 2343: before your own server.  This is the natural order for walking the chain
 2344: when composing a forwarded abuse report.
 2345: 
 2346: =item *
 2347: 
 2348: C<ip> may be C<undef> for a hop that nonetheless has a valid C<for> or
 2349: C<id> field -- for example, a C<Received:> header added by a local
 2350: delivery agent that does not record an IP.  Always test C<defined
 2351: $hop-E<gt>{ip}> before using it.
 2352: 
 2353: =item *
 2354: 
 2355: C<for> and C<id> are C<undef>, not the empty string, when absent.  C<ip>
 2356: is also C<undef>, not C<'(unknown)'> as in some other methods.  All four
 2357: fields must be tested with C<defined>, not boolean truthiness, to
 2358: distinguish between absent and empty.
 2359: 
 2360: =item *
 2361: 
 2362: C<report()> applies an additional filter when displaying this data: it only
 2363: shows hops where C<id> or C<for> is defined, suppressing hops where only
 2364: an IP was found.  C<received_trail()> itself returns all hops with any
 2365: extractable data, including IP-only hops, giving callers the full picture.
 2366: 
 2367: =item *
 2368: 
 2369: The C<received> field is the unfolded header value as stored after RFC 2822
 2370: line-folding is removed during C<parse_email()>.  Continuation whitespace
 2371: is replaced with a single space; the value will not contain embedded
 2372: newlines.
 2373: 
 2374: =back
 2375: 
 2376: =head3 API Specification
 2377: 
 2378: =head4 Input
 2379: 
 2380:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 2381:     # No arguments.
 2382:     []
 2383: 
 2384: =head4 Output
 2385: 
 2386:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 2387: 
 2388:     # A list (possibly empty) of hashrefs, oldest-hop first:
 2389:     (
 2390:         {
 2391:             type => HASHREF,
 2392:             keys => {
 2393:                 received => {
 2394:                     type => SCALAR,
 2395:                     # Complete unfolded Received: header value; always defined.
 2396:                 },
 2397:                 ip => {
 2398:                     type     => SCALAR,
 2399:                     optional => 1,  # present but may be undef
 2400:                     regex    => qr/^\d{1,3}(?:\.\d{1,3}){3}$/,
 2401:                 },
 2402:                 for => {
 2403:                     type     => SCALAR,
 2404:                     optional => 1,  # present but may be undef
 2405:                     # Fully-qualified email address: local@domain.tld
 2406:                     regex    => qr/^[^\s@]+\@[\w.-]+\.[a-zA-Z]{2,}$/,
 2407:                 },
 2408:                 id => {
 2409:                     type     => SCALAR,
 2410:                     optional => 1,  # present but may be undef
 2411:                     regex    => qr/^[\w.-]+$/,
 2412:                 },
 2413:             },
 2414:         },
 2415:         # ... one hashref per hop with at least one extractable field,
 2416:         #     in oldest-first (outermost relay first) order
 2417:     )
 2418: 
 2419:     # Empty list when no Received: headers are present or none yielded
 2420:     # any extractable data.
 2421: 
 2422: =cut
 2423: 
 2424: sub received_trail {
 2425: 	my $self = $_[0];
 2426: 
 2427: 	return @{ $self->{_rcvd_tracking} };
 2428: }
 2429: 
 2430: =head2 risk_assessment()
 2431: 
 2432: Evaluates the message against a set of heuristic checks and returns an
 2433: overall risk level, a weighted numeric score, and a list of every specific
 2434: red flag that contributed to the score.
 2435: 
 2436: The assessment covers five categories: originating IP characteristics, email
 2437: authentication results, C<Date:> header validity, identity and header
 2438: consistency, and URL and domain properties.  Each finding is assigned a
 2439: severity, a machine-readable flag name, and a human-readable detail string.
 2440: 
 2441: The result is computed once and cached; subsequent calls on the same object
 2442: return the same hashref without repeating any analysis.  Calling
 2443: C<risk_assessment()> also implicitly triggers C<originating_ip()>,
 2444: C<embedded_urls()>, and C<mailto_domains()> if they have not already been
 2445: called, performing all associated network I/O.
 2446: 
 2447: =head3 Usage
 2448: 
 2449:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 2450:     my $risk = $analyser->risk_assessment();
 2451: 
 2452:     printf "Risk level : %s (score: %d)\n", $risk->{level}, $risk->{score};
 2453: 
 2454:     for my $f (@{ $risk->{flags} }) {
 2455:         printf "  [%-6s] %s\n    %s\n",
 2456:             $f->{severity}, $f->{flag}, $f->{detail};
 2457:     }
 2458: 
 2459:     # Gate an automated report on HIGH level only
 2460:     if ($risk->{level} eq 'HIGH') {
 2461:         send_abuse_report($analyser->abuse_report_text());
 2462:     }
 2463: 
 2464:     # Collect only HIGH and MEDIUM flags for a summary
 2465:     my @significant = grep { $_->{severity} =~ /^(?:HIGH|MEDIUM)$/ }
 2466:                       @{ $risk->{flags} };
 2467: 
 2468:     # Check for a specific flag
 2469:     my ($flag) = grep { $_->{flag} eq 'recently_registered_domain' }
 2470:                  @{ $risk->{flags} };
 2471:     warn "Phishing domain suspected\n" if $flag;
 2472: 
 2473:     # INFO level means no actionable red flags
 2474:     if ($risk->{level} eq 'INFO') {
 2475:         print "No significant red flags detected.\n";
 2476:     }
 2477: 
 2478: =head3 Arguments
 2479: 
 2480: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 2481: 
 2482: =head3 Returns
 2483: 
 2484: Returns a hashref with an overall risk level and a list of specific
 2485: red flags found in the message:
 2486: 
 2487:     {
 2488:         level => 'HIGH',          # HIGH | MEDIUM | LOW | INFO
 2489:         score => 7,               # raw weighted score
 2490:         flags => [
 2491:             { severity => 'HIGH',   flag => 'recently_registered_domain',
 2492:               detail => 'firmluminary.com registered 2025-09-01 (< 180 days ago)' },
 2493:             { severity => 'MEDIUM', flag => 'residential_sending_ip',
 2494:               detail => 'rDNS 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au looks like a broadband line' },
 2495:             { severity => 'MEDIUM', flag => 'url_shortener',
 2496:               detail => 'bit.ly used - real destination hidden' },
 2497:             ...
 2498:         ],
 2499:     }
 2500: 
 2501: A hashref with exactly three keys, all always present:
 2502: 
 2503: =over 4
 2504: 
 2505: =item C<level> (string)
 2506: 
 2507: The overall risk classification, determined by the weighted score:
 2508: 
 2509:     Score >= 9  =>  'HIGH'
 2510:     Score >= 5  =>  'MEDIUM'
 2511:     Score >= 2  =>  'LOW'
 2512:     Score <  2  =>  'INFO'
 2513: 
 2514: C<'INFO'> means either no flags were raised or only zero-weight (INFO
 2515: severity) flags were raised.  It does not mean the message is definitely
 2516: legitimate; it means no significant heuristic evidence of spam was found.
 2517: 
 2518: =item C<score> (integer)
 2519: 
 2520: The sum of the weights of all flags raised.  Weights by severity:
 2521: 
 2522:     HIGH   => 3
 2523:     MEDIUM => 2
 2524:     LOW    => 1
 2525:     INFO   => 0
 2526: 
 2527: The score is a non-negative integer.  Multiple flags of the same severity
 2528: each contribute their full weight independently; there is no cap on the
 2529: score.
 2530: 
 2531: =item C<flags> (arrayref of hashrefs)
 2532: 
 2533: A reference to a list of flag hashrefs, one per red flag raised, in the
 2534: order they were detected.  Each hashref contains exactly three keys:
 2535: 
 2536: =over 8
 2537: 
 2538: =item C<severity> (string)
 2539: 
 2540: One of C<'HIGH'>, C<'MEDIUM'>, C<'LOW'>, or C<'INFO'>.
 2541: 
 2542: =item C<flag> (string)
 2543: 
 2544: A lower-cased, underscore-separated machine-readable identifier.  See the
 2545: Algorithm section for the full list of possible flag names.
 2546: 
 2547: =item C<detail> (string)
 2548: 
 2549: A human-readable sentence describing the specific finding, including the
 2550: values from the message that triggered the flag (domain name, IP address,
 2551: header value, etc.).  Suitable for inclusion in an abuse report or log.
 2552: 
 2553: =back
 2554: 
 2555: The arrayref is empty (C<[]>) when no flags are raised.
 2556: 
 2557: =back
 2558: 
 2559: =head3 Side Effects
 2560: 
 2561: The first call triggers C<originating_ip()>, C<embedded_urls()>, and
 2562: C<mailto_domains()> if they have not already run on the current message.
 2563: Each of those methods may perform network I/O as documented in their own
 2564: entries.  Specifically:
 2565: 
 2566: =over 4
 2567: 
 2568: =item * C<originating_ip()> performs a PTR lookup and RDAP/WHOIS for the
 2569: sending IP.
 2570: 
 2571: =item * C<embedded_urls()> performs an A lookup and RDAP/WHOIS for each
 2572: unique URL hostname.
 2573: 
 2574: =item * C<mailto_domains()> performs A, MX, NS, and WHOIS queries for
 2575: each unique contact domain.
 2576: 
 2577: =back
 2578: 
 2579: All results are cached.  Subsequent calls to C<risk_assessment()> on the
 2580: same object return the cached hashref immediately.  The cache is invalidated
 2581: by C<parse_email()>.
 2582: 
 2583: =head3 Algorithm: flags and scoring
 2584: 
 2585: The following flags may be raised.  They are evaluated in five groups, in
 2586: the order shown.  The same flag name is never raised more than once per
 2587: message.
 2588: 
 2589: B<Group 1 -- Originating IP> (requires C<originating_ip()> to return a
 2590: result):
 2591: 
 2592: =over 4
 2593: 
 2594: =item C<residential_sending_ip> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2595: 
 2596: The rDNS of the sending IP matches patterns associated with residential
 2597: broadband or dynamically-assigned addresses: an embedded dotted-quad, or
 2598: any of the substrings C<dsl>, C<adsl>, C<cable>, C<broad>, C<dial>,
 2599: C<dynamic>, C<dhcp>, C<ppp>, C<residential>, C<cust>, C<home>, C<pool>,
 2600: C<client>, C<user>, C<staticN>, or C<hostN>.
 2601: 
 2602: =item C<no_reverse_dns> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2603: 
 2604: The sending IP has no PTR record, or the PTR lookup returned the sentinel
 2605: C<'(no reverse DNS)'>.  Legitimate mail servers invariably have rDNS.
 2606: 
 2607: =item C<low_confidence_origin> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2608: 
 2609: The originating IP was taken from an unverified header (C<X-Originating-IP>)
 2610: rather than from the C<Received:> chain.  Confidence level is C<'low'>.
 2611: 
 2612: =item C<high_spam_country> (INFO, weight 0)
 2613: 
 2614: The sending IP's country code is one of: C<CN> (China), C<RU> (Russia),
 2615: C<NG> (Nigeria), C<VN> (Vietnam), C<IN> (India), C<PK> (Pakistan),
 2616: C<BD> (Bangladesh).  Informational only; does not contribute to the score.
 2617: 
 2618: =back
 2619: 
 2620: B<Group 2 -- Email authentication> (from C<Authentication-Results:> header):
 2621: 
 2622: =over 4
 2623: 
 2624: =item C<spf_fail> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2625: 
 2626: SPF result is C<fail>, C<permerror>, C<temperror>, C<none>, or any value
 2627: other than C<pass> or C<softfail>.  The sending IP is not authorised by
 2628: the domain's SPF record.
 2629: 
 2630: =item C<spf_softfail> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2631: 
 2632: SPF result is C<softfail> (C<~all>).  The sending IP is not explicitly
 2633: authorised but the domain policy does not hard-fail it.
 2634: 
 2635: =item C<dkim_fail> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2636: 
 2637: DKIM result is present and is any value other than C<pass>.
 2638: 
 2639: =item C<dmarc_fail> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2640: 
 2641: DMARC result is present and is any value other than C<pass>.
 2642: 
 2643: =item C<dkim_domain_mismatch> (INFO or MEDIUM, weight 0 or 2)
 2644: 
 2645: The DKIM signing domain (C<d=> tag) differs from the registrable domain
 2646: of the C<From:> address.  Raised at INFO (weight 0) when DKIM passes --
 2647: this is normal for bulk senders using ESPs such as SendGrid or Mailchimp.
 2648: Raised at MEDIUM (weight 2) when DKIM fails or is absent -- a differing
 2649: domain combined with a failed signature is more suspicious.
 2650: 
 2651: =back
 2652: 
 2653: B<Group 3 -- Date: header>:
 2654: 
 2655: =over 4
 2656: 
 2657: =item C<missing_date> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2658: 
 2659: No C<Date:> header is present, or it contains only whitespace.  Violates
 2660: RFC 5322; common in programmatically-generated spam.
 2661: 
 2662: =item C<suspicious_date> (LOW, weight 1)
 2663: 
 2664: The C<Date:> header is present but more than 7 days in the past or more
 2665: than 7 days in the future relative to the time of analysis.  Timezone
 2666: offsets are ignored during comparison (maximum error: approximately 14
 2667: hours, well within the 7-day window).
 2668: 
 2669: =back
 2670: 
 2671: B<Group 4 -- Header identity and consistency>:
 2672: 
 2673: =over 4
 2674: 
 2675: =item C<display_name_domain_spoof> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2676: 
 2677: The C<From:> display name contains a domain name (matched against the
 2678: suffixes C<.com>, C<.net>, C<.org>, C<.io>, C<.co>, C<.uk>, C<.au>,
 2679: C<.gov>, C<.edu>) that differs at the registrable level from the actual
 2680: C<From:> address domain.  Example: C<"PayPal paypal.com" E<lt>phish@evil.exampleE<gt>>.
 2681: 
 2682: =item C<free_webmail_sender> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2683: 
 2684: The C<From:> address belongs to a free webmail provider: Gmail, Yahoo,
 2685: Hotmail, Outlook, Live, AOL, ProtonMail, Yandex, or mail.ru.
 2686: 
 2687: =item C<reply_to_differs_from_from> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2688: 
 2689: A C<Reply-To:> header is present and its email address differs from the
 2690: C<From:> address (case-insensitive comparison).  Replies will be harvested
 2691: by a different address than the apparent sender.
 2692: 
 2693: =item C<undisclosed_recipients> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2694: 
 2695: The C<To:> header is absent, empty, contains the string C<undisclosed>, or
 2696: matches the group-syntax sentinel C<:;>.
 2697: 
 2698: =item C<encoded_subject> (LOW, weight 1)
 2699: 
 2700: The C<Subject:> header contains a MIME encoded-word sequence
 2701: (C<=?charset?encoding?text?=>).  Often used to evade keyword filters.
 2702: 
 2703: =back
 2704: 
 2705: B<Group 5 -- URLs and domains> (from C<embedded_urls()> and
 2706: C<mailto_domains()>):
 2707: 
 2708: =over 4
 2709: 
 2710: =item C<url_shortener> (MEDIUM, weight 2)
 2711: 
 2712: At least one URL hostname is in the built-in URL shortener list (over 25
 2713: services including C<bit.ly>, C<tinyurl.com>, C<t.co>, C<ow.ly>, etc.).
 2714: Raised at most once per unique shortener hostname per message.
 2715: 
 2716: =item C<http_not_https> (LOW, weight 1)
 2717: 
 2718: At least one URL uses the plain C<http://> scheme rather than C<https://>.
 2719: Raised at most once per unique hostname.
 2720: 
 2721: =item C<recently_registered_domain> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2722: 
 2723: At least one contact domain was registered less than 180 days before the
 2724: time of analysis.
 2725: 
 2726: =item C<domain_expires_soon> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2727: 
 2728: At least one contact domain expires within the next 30 days.  Suggests a
 2729: throwaway domain.
 2730: 
 2731: =item C<domain_expired> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2732: 
 2733: At least one contact domain has already passed its expiry date.
 2734: 
 2735: =item C<lookalike_domain> (HIGH, weight 3)
 2736: 
 2737: At least one contact domain contains the name of a well-known brand
 2738: (C<paypal>, C<apple>, C<google>, C<amazon>, C<microsoft>, C<netflix>,
 2739: C<ebay>, C<instagram>, C<facebook>, C<twitter>, C<linkedin>,
 2740: C<bankofamerica>, C<wellsfargo>, C<chase>, C<barclays>, C<hsbc>,
 2741: C<lloyds>, C<santander>) but is not the brand's own canonical domain
 2742: (e.g. C<paypal.com>, C<paypal.co.uk>).
 2743: 
 2744: =back
 2745: 
 2746: =head3 Notes
 2747: 
 2748: =over 4
 2749: 
 2750: =item *
 2751: 
 2752: The C<flags> arrayref is a reference to the module's internal list.
 2753: Callers must not modify it.  To iterate safely, use C<@{ $risk-E<gt>{flags} }>.
 2754: 
 2755: =item *
 2756: 
 2757: Flags are not deduplicated across categories.  If C<spf_fail> and
 2758: C<dkim_fail> both apply, both appear in the list and both contribute to
 2759: the score.
 2760: 
 2761: =item *
 2762: 
 2763: C<high_spam_country> and C<dkim_domain_mismatch> (when DKIM passes)
 2764: contribute zero to the score.  Their presence does not change the level
 2765: classification, but they appear in the C<flags> list so callers can
 2766: include them in reports.
 2767: 
 2768: =item *
 2769: 
 2770: The level thresholds are fixed constants: HIGH >= 9, MEDIUM >= 5, LOW >= 2,
 2771: INFO < 2.  They are not configurable.
 2772: 
 2773: =item *
 2774: 
 2775: C<risk_assessment()> does not directly raise flags for domains found only
 2776: in URLs (C<embedded_urls()> hosts); domain checks in Group 5 apply only
 2777: to domains from C<mailto_domains()>.  URL hostname checks (shorteners,
 2778: HTTP) use the C<embedded_urls()> list.
 2779: 
 2780: =item *
 2781: 
 2782: If C<parse_email()> has not been called, or was called with an empty or
 2783: malformed message, C<risk_assessment()> returns a valid hashref with
 2784: C<level =E<gt> 'INFO'>, C<score =E<gt> 0>, and C<flags =E<gt> []>.
 2785: 
 2786: =back
 2787: 
 2788: =head3 API Specification
 2789: 
 2790: =head4 Input
 2791: 
 2792:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 2793:     # No arguments.
 2794:     []
 2795: 
 2796: =head4 Output
 2797: 
 2798:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 2799:     {
 2800:         type => HASHREF,
 2801:         keys => {
 2802:             level => {
 2803:                 type  => SCALAR,
 2804:                 regex => qr/^(?:HIGH|MEDIUM|LOW|INFO)$/,
 2805:             },
 2806:             score => {
 2807:                 type  => SCALAR,
 2808:                 regex => qr/^\d+$/,  # non-negative integer
 2809:             },
 2810:             flags => {
 2811:                 type => ARRAYREF,
 2812:                 # Reference to a list (possibly empty) of hashrefs:
 2813:                 # [
 2814:                 #   {
 2815:                 #     severity => qr/^(?:HIGH|MEDIUM|LOW|INFO)$/,
 2816:                 #     flag     => qr/^[a-z][a-z0-9_]+$/,
 2817:                 #     detail   => SCALAR,  # human-readable string
 2818:                 #   },
 2819:                 #   ...
 2820:                 # ]
 2821:             },
 2822:         },
 2823:     }
 2824: 
 2825: =cut

 3085: 
 3086: =head2 abuse_report_text()
 3087: 
 3088: Produces a compact, plain-text string intended to be sent as the body of
 3089: an abuse report email to an ISP or hosting provider.  It summarises the
 3090: risk level, lists every red flag with its detail, identifies the originating
 3091: IP and its network owner, lists the abuse contacts, and appends the complete
 3092: message headers so the recipient can trace the session in their own logs.
 3093: 
 3094: The message body is intentionally omitted to keep the report concise.
 3095: Headers are sufficient for an ISP to locate the relevant mail session; the
 3096: body adds bulk without aiding the investigation.
 3097: 
 3098: This method is the companion to C<abuse_contacts()>: call
 3099: C<abuse_contacts()> to obtain the addresses to send the report to, and
 3100: C<abuse_report_text()> to obtain the text to send.  Use C<report()> instead
 3101: when you want a comprehensive analyst-facing document rather than a
 3102: send-ready ISP report.
 3103: 
 3104: =head3 Usage
 3105: 
 3106:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 3107: 
 3108:     my $text     = $analyser->abuse_report_text();
 3109:     my @contacts = $analyser->abuse_contacts();
 3110: 
 3111:     for my $c (@contacts) {
 3112:         send_email(
 3113:             to      => $c->{address},
 3114:             subject => 'Abuse report: ' . ($analyser->originating_ip()->{ip} // 'unknown'),
 3115:             body    => $text,
 3116:         );
 3117:     }
 3118: 
 3119:     # Print to stdout for manual review before sending
 3120:     print $text;
 3121: 
 3122:     # Write to file for a ticketing system
 3123:     open my $fh, '>', 'abuse_report.txt' or die $!;
 3124:     print $fh $text;
 3125:     close $fh;
 3126: 
 3127: =head3 Arguments
 3128: 
 3129: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 3130: 
 3131: =head3 Returns
 3132: 
 3133: A plain scalar string containing the report text.  The string is
 3134: newline-terminated and uses Unix line endings (C<\n>) throughout.
 3135: The string is never empty; it always contains at least the boilerplate
 3136: introduction and the risk-level line, even if no red flags were found.
 3137: 
 3138: The report is structured as follows, in order:
 3139: 
 3140: =over 4
 3141: 
 3142: =item 1. Introduction
 3143: 
 3144: Two fixed lines:
 3145: 
 3146:     This is an automated abuse report generated by Email::Abuse::Investigator.
 3147:     Please investigate the following spam/phishing message.
 3148: 
 3149: =item 2. Risk level
 3150: 
 3151:     RISK LEVEL: HIGH (score: 11)
 3152: 
 3153: =item 3. Red flags (omitted if no flags were raised)
 3154: 
 3155:     RED FLAGS IDENTIFIED:
 3156:       [HIGH] firmluminary.com was registered 2025-09-01 (less than 180 days ago)
 3157:       [MEDIUM] rDNS 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au looks like a broadband line
 3158:       ...
 3159: 
 3160: Each flag is formatted as C<[SEVERITY] detail-string>, one per line,
 3161: indented two spaces.  The flag machine-name is not included; only the
 3162: human-readable detail string is shown, matching what a postmaster would
 3163: want to read.
 3164: 
 3165: =item 4. Originating IP (omitted if C<originating_ip()> returns C<undef>)
 3166: 
 3167:     ORIGINATING IP: 120.88.161.249 (120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au)
 3168:     NETWORK OWNER:  TPG Telecom Limited
 3169: 
 3170: =item 5. Abuse contacts (omitted if C<abuse_contacts()> returns an empty list)
 3171: 
 3172:     ABUSE CONTACTS:
 3173:       abuse@tpg.com.au (Sending ISP)
 3174:       abuse@registrar.example (Domain registrar for firmluminary.com)
 3175: 
 3176: =item 6. Original message headers
 3177: 
 3178:     ------------------------------------------------------------------------
 3179:     ORIGINAL MESSAGE HEADERS:
 3180:     ------------------------------------------------------------------------
 3181:     received: from 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au ...
 3182:     from: Sender <spammer@firmluminary.com>
 3183:     ...
 3184: 
 3185: All parsed headers are emitted, one per line, in the order they appeared
 3186: in the original message.  Header names are lower-cased (as normalised
 3187: during C<parse_email()>).  Header values are verbatim.  The message
 3188: body is not included.
 3189: 
 3190: =back
 3191: 
 3192: =head3 Side Effects
 3193: 
 3194: Calls C<risk_assessment()>, C<originating_ip()>, and C<abuse_contacts()>
 3195: if they have not already run, which in turn may perform network I/O as
 3196: documented in those methods.  All results are cached; the text is not
 3197: itself cached, but re-computing it is cheap since all the underlying data
 3198: is already cached.
 3199: 
 3200: =head3 Notes
 3201: 
 3202: =over 4
 3203: 
 3204: =item *
 3205: 
 3206: Header names in the output are lower-cased (e.g. C<from:>, C<received:>),
 3207: because that is how they are stored internally after C<parse_email()>
 3208: normalises them.  Postmasters are accustomed to receiving headers in their
 3209: original mixed case; if canonical capitalisation is required, a simple
 3210: substitution (C<s/^([\w-]+)/\u\L$1/>) will restore it.
 3211: 
 3212: =item *
 3213: 
 3214: The message body is deliberately excluded.  This avoids transmitting
 3215: potentially malicious or offensive content to third parties, keeps the
 3216: report below common size limits for abuse mailboxes, and is consistent
 3217: with the RFC 2646 / ARF (Abuse Reporting Format) practice of including
 3218: only the headers in a first-contact report.  To include the body, callers
 3219: can append C<$self-E<gt>{_raw}> directly, though this is not recommended.
 3220: 
 3221: =item *
 3222: 
 3223: The separator lines are exactly 72 hyphens (C<-> x 72), matching the
 3224: separator width used by C<report()>.
 3225: 
 3226: =item *
 3227: 
 3228: The output is suitable for use as a plain-text email body.  It is not
 3229: ARF (RFC 5965) compliant; it does not include a C<message/feedback-report>
 3230: MIME part.  For ARF-compliant reporting, use the output of this method as
 3231: the human-readable first part and add the ARF metadata separately.
 3232: 
 3233: =item *
 3234: 
 3235: If C<parse_email()> has not been called, all sections that depend on
 3236: analysis will be empty (no flags, no originating IP, no contacts) and the
 3237: header section will be blank.  The method will not die.
 3238: 
 3239: =back
 3240: 
 3241: =head3 API Specification
 3242: 
 3243: =head4 Input
 3244: 
 3245:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 3246:     # No arguments.
 3247:     []
 3248: 
 3249: =head4 Output
 3250: 
 3251:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 3252:     {
 3253:         type  => SCALAR,
 3254:         # Non-empty plain-text string, newline-terminated.
 3255:         # Always defined; never undef.
 3256:         # Line endings: Unix LF (\n) only.
 3257:         # Minimum content: introduction + risk-level line.
 3258:     }
 3259: 
 3260: =cut
 3261:

 3322: 
 3323: =head2 abuse_contacts()
 3324: 
 3325: Collates the complete set of parties that should receive an abuse report
 3326: for this message: the ISP that owns the sending IP, the operators of every
 3327: URL host, the web, mail, and DNS hosts of every contact domain, each
 3328: domain's registrar, the webmail or ESP account provider identified from
 3329: key headers, the DKIM signing organisation, and the ESP identified via
 3330: the C<List-Unsubscribe:> header.
 3331: 
 3332: For each party the method produces the role description, the abuse email
 3333: address, a supporting note, and the source of the information.  Addresses
 3334: are deduplicated globally: if the same address is discovered through
 3335: multiple routes (e.g. Google as both the sending ISP and the owner of a
 3336: blogspot.com URL in the message body), it appears only once.  The C<role>
 3337: string for that entry is the combined description of all routes that found
 3338: it, joined by C<" and ">, and the C<roles> key holds the individual role
 3339: strings as an arrayref.
 3340: 
 3341: This method is designed to be used together with C<abuse_report_text()>:
 3342: iterate over the returned contacts to obtain the list of addresses, and
 3343: send the text from C<abuse_report_text()> to each one.
 3344: 
 3345: =head3 Usage
 3346: 
 3347:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 3348:     my @contacts = $analyser->abuse_contacts();
 3349: 
 3350:     for my $c (@contacts) {
 3351:         printf "Role    : %s\n", $c->{role};
 3352:         printf "Send to : %s\n", $c->{address};
 3353:         printf "Note    : %s\n", $c->{note}  if $c->{note};
 3354:         printf "Source  : %s\n", $c->{via};
 3355:         print  "\n";
 3356:     }
 3357: 
 3358:     # Collect addresses for sending
 3359:     my @addresses = map { $_->{address} } @contacts;
 3360: 
 3361:     # Filter to WHOIS-discovered contacts only
 3362:     my @whois_contacts = grep { $_->{via} =~ /whois/ } @contacts;
 3363: 
 3364:     # Check whether any registrar abuse contacts were found
 3365:     my @registrar = grep { $_->{role} =~ /registrar/ } @contacts;
 3366: 
 3367: =head3 Arguments
 3368: 
 3369: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 3370: 
 3371: =head3 Returns
 3372: 
 3373: A list (not an arrayref) of hashrefs, one per unique abuse contact address,
 3374: in the order they were first discovered.  Returns an empty list if no
 3375: actionable abuse contacts can be determined, or if C<parse_email()> has
 3376: not been called.
 3377: 
 3378: Returns a de-duplicated list of hashrefs, one per party that should
 3379: receive an abuse report, in priority order:
 3380: 
 3381:     {
 3382:         role    => 'Sending ISP',          # human-readable role
 3383:         address => 'abuse@senderisp.example',
 3384:         note    => 'IP block 120.88.0.0/14 owner',
 3385:         via     => 'ip-whois',             # ip-whois | domain-whois | provider-table | rdap
 3386:     }
 3387: 
 3388: Roles produced (in order):
 3389: 
 3390:   Sending ISP            - network owner of the originating IP
 3391:   URL host               - network owner of each unique web-server IP
 3392:   Mail host (MX)         - network owner of the domain's MX record IP
 3393:   DNS host (NS)          - network owner of the authoritative NS IP
 3394:   Domain registrar       - registrar abuse contact from domain WHOIS
 3395:   Account provider       - e.g. Gmail / Outlook for the From:/Sender: account
 3396:   DKIM signer            - the organisation whose key signed the message
 3397:   ESP / bulk sender      - identified via List-Unsubscribe: domain
 3398: 
 3399: Addresses are deduplicated so the same address never appears twice,
 3400: even if it is discovered through multiple routes.
 3401: 
 3402: Each hashref contains the following keys, all always present:
 3403: 
 3404: =over 4
 3405: 
 3406: =item C<role> (string)
 3407: 
 3408: A human-readable description of the party's relationship to the message.
 3409: When the same address was found via multiple discovery routes, the role
 3410: strings from each route are joined with C<" and "> (e.g.
 3411: C<"Sending ISP (provider table) and URL host (provider table)">).
 3412: See the Algorithm section for the full set of role string patterns.
 3413: 
 3414: =item C<roles> (arrayref of strings)
 3415: 
 3416: The individual role strings for each discovery route that found this
 3417: address, in discovery order.  Contains exactly one element when the
 3418: address was found via a single route; two or more elements when multiple
 3419: routes converged on the same address.  The C<role> key is always the
 3420: C<join(' and ', @{$c->{roles}})> of this arrayref.
 3421: 
 3422: =item C<address> (string)
 3423: 
 3424: The abuse contact email address, lower-cased.  Always contains an C<@>
 3425: sign.  Deduplicated globally: each distinct address appears at most once
 3426: across the entire list, regardless of how many discovery routes found it.
 3427: 
 3428: =item C<note> (string)
 3429: 
 3430: Supporting information about why this party was identified and what action
 3431: to request.  For provider-table entries this is the note from the built-in
 3432: table (which may include a URL to a web-based abuse form).  For WHOIS- and
 3433: RDAP-discovered entries this describes the IP block or domain involved.
 3434: Always defined; may be the empty string for entries where no note is
 3435: available.  When roles are merged, this reflects the note from the first
 3436: discovery route.
 3437: 
 3438: =item C<via> (string)
 3439: 
 3440: The discovery method for the first route that found this address.  One of:
 3441: 
 3442: =over 8
 3443: 
 3444: =item C<'provider-table'>
 3445: 
 3446: The address was found in the module's built-in table of well-known
 3447: providers (Google, Microsoft, Cloudflare, SendGrid, Mailchimp, etc.).
 3448: Provider-table addresses take priority over WHOIS for the same entity
 3449: because they are curated and point to the right team, whereas generic
 3450: WHOIS contacts sometimes route to NOCs rather than abuse desks.
 3451: 
 3452: =item C<'ip-whois'>
 3453: 
 3454: The address was obtained from an RDAP or WHOIS lookup on an IP block
 3455: (the sending IP, a URL host IP, or an MX/NS IP).
 3456: 
 3457: =item C<'domain-whois'>
 3458: 
 3459: The address was obtained from a WHOIS lookup on a domain name (registrar
 3460: abuse contact from the C<Registrar Abuse Contact Email:> or equivalent
 3461: field).
 3462: 
 3463: =back
 3464: 
 3465: =back
 3466: 
 3467: =head3 Side Effects
 3468: 
 3469: Triggers C<originating_ip()>, C<embedded_urls()>, and C<mailto_domains()>
 3470: if they have not already run on the current message, performing all
 3471: associated network I/O as documented in those methods.  Additionally
 3472: consults the built-in provider table and the cached authentication results;
 3473: neither requires network I/O.
 3474: 
 3475: The result is not independently cached.  Each call recomputes the contact
 3476: list from the cached results of the underlying methods.  Because those
 3477: results are cached, subsequent calls are fast (no network I/O), but they
 3478: do re-execute the collation and deduplication logic.
 3479: 
 3480: =head3 Algorithm: discovery routes
 3481: 
 3482: Contacts are discovered through six routes, applied in order.
 3483: Deduplication is global across all routes: if an address is found by
 3484: more than one route, a single entry is kept and the role strings from
 3485: every route that found it are accumulated into C<roles> and joined into
 3486: C<role>.  An entry is suppressed entirely if its address is empty, does
 3487: not contain an C<@> sign, or is the sentinel C<'(unknown)'>.
 3488: 
 3489: =over 4
 3490: 
 3491: =item Route 1 -- Sending ISP
 3492: 
 3493: The originating IP from C<originating_ip()> is looked up in the built-in
 3494: provider table (by rDNS hostname, stripping subdomains until a match is
 3495: found).  If found, a C<provider-table> entry is added with role
 3496: C<"Sending ISP (provider table)">.
 3497: 
 3498: The C<abuse> field from C<originating_ip()> (obtained from RDAP/WHOIS) is
 3499: then added as an C<ip-whois> entry with role C<"Sending ISP">, unless it
 3500: is C<'(unknown)'>.
 3501: 
 3502: =item Route 2 -- URL hosts
 3503: 
 3504: For each unique hostname in C<embedded_urls()>, the built-in provider
 3505: table is consulted (by hostname, stripping subdomains).  If found, a
 3506: C<provider-table> entry is added with role C<"URL host (provider table)">.
 3507: 
 3508: The C<abuse> field from the URL hashref is then added as an C<ip-whois>
 3509: entry with role C<"URL host">, unless it is C<'(unknown)'>.
 3510: 
 3511: Each unique hostname is processed at most once; multiple URLs on the same
 3512: host do not generate multiple contacts.
 3513: 
 3514: =item Route 3 -- Contact domain hosting and registration
 3515: 
 3516: For each domain from C<mailto_domains()>, up to four contacts may be
 3517: generated:
 3518: 
 3519: =over 8
 3520: 
 3521: =item *
 3522: 
 3523: B<Web host>: if C<web_abuse> is present, both a provider-table lookup
 3524: on the domain name and the WHOIS-derived C<web_abuse> address are tried.
 3525: Role: C<"Web host of $domain"> or C<"Web host of $domain (provider table)">.
 3526: 
 3527: =item *
 3528: 
 3529: B<Mail host (MX)>: if C<mx_abuse> is present.
 3530: Role: C<"Mail host (MX) for $domain">, via C<ip-whois>.
 3531: 
 3532: =item *
 3533: 
 3534: B<DNS host (NS)>: if C<ns_abuse> is present.
 3535: Role: C<"DNS host (NS) for $domain">, via C<ip-whois>.
 3536: 
 3537: =item *
 3538: 
 3539: B<Domain registrar>: if C<registrar_abuse> is present.
 3540: Role: C<"Domain registrar for $domain">, via C<domain-whois>.
 3541: 
 3542: =back
 3543: 
 3544: =item Route 4 -- Account provider
 3545: 
 3546: The C<From:>, C<Reply-To:>, C<Return-Path:>, and C<Sender:> header values
 3547: are inspected in that order.  The domain portion of each address is looked
 3548: up in the built-in provider table (stripping subdomains until a match).
 3549: If found, a C<provider-table> entry is added with role
 3550: C<"Account provider ($header: $value)">.  This identifies the webmail
 3551: or ESP service that hosts the sender's account.
 3552: 
 3553: =item Route 5 -- DKIM signing organisation
 3554: 
 3555: The C<d=> tag from the C<DKIM-Signature:> header is looked up in the
 3556: built-in provider table.  If found, a C<provider-table> entry is added
 3557: with role C<"DKIM signer (provider table): $domain">.  The full domain
 3558: pipeline (web/MX/NS/WHOIS) for this domain is already handled via Route 3
 3559: through C<mailto_domains()>.
 3560: 
 3561: =item Route 6 -- ESP / bulk sender (List-Unsubscribe)
 3562: 
 3563: Both C<https://> URLs and C<mailto:> addresses in the C<List-Unsubscribe:>
 3564: header are parsed for their domains.  Each unique domain is looked up in
 3565: the built-in provider table.  If found, a C<provider-table> entry is added
 3566: with role C<"ESP / bulk sender (List-Unsubscribe: $domain)">.
 3567: 
 3568: =back
 3569: 
 3570: =head3 Notes
 3571: 
 3572: =over 4
 3573: 
 3574: =item *
 3575: 
 3576: Deduplication is by lower-cased address only.  Two contacts with different
 3577: roles but the same address result in a single entry using the data from
 3578: whichever route found it first.  The later route's role and note are
 3579: silently discarded.
 3580: 
 3581: =item *
 3582: 
 3583: The provider table contains curated entries for approximately 50
 3584: well-known domains including major webmail providers (Gmail, Outlook,
 3585: Yahoo, Apple), CDNs and hosters (Cloudflare, Fastly, Akamai, AWS,
 3586: DigitalOcean, Vultr, Hetzner, Contabo, Leaseweb, M247, OVH, Linode),
 3587: ESPs (SendGrid, Mailchimp, Mailgun, Postmark, Brevo, Klaviyo, Campaign
 3588: Monitor, Constant Contact, HubSpot), registrars (GoDaddy, Namecheap),
 3589: and ISPs (TPG, Internode).  Subdomain matching strips labels left-to-right
 3590: until a match is found, so C<mail.sendgrid.net> matches C<sendgrid.net>.
 3591: 
 3592: =item *
 3593: 
 3594: Provider-table entries take priority in the sense that they are added
 3595: first; if the WHOIS address happens to match the provider-table address,
 3596: the WHOIS entry is suppressed by deduplication.  If they differ (unusual
 3597: but possible), both are added.
 3598: 
 3599: =item *
 3600: 
 3601: The result is not cached.  If you call C<abuse_contacts()> multiple times
 3602: on the same object, the full collation runs each time.  If this is a
 3603: concern, store the result in a variable:
 3604: C<my @contacts = $analyser-E<gt>abuse_contacts()>.
 3605: 
 3606: =item *
 3607: 
 3608: An empty list is returned if the message has no usable originating IP, no
 3609: extractable URLs, no contact domains, and no recognised provider-table
 3610: matches.  This is unusual in practice but can occur for very sparse or
 3611: malformed messages.
 3612: 
 3613: =back
 3614: 
 3615: =head3 API Specification
 3616: 
 3617: =head4 Input
 3618: 
 3619:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 3620:     # No arguments.
 3621:     []
 3622: 
 3623: =head4 Output
 3624: 
 3625:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 3626: 
 3627:     # A list (possibly empty) of hashrefs, in discovery order:
 3628:     (
 3629:         {
 3630:             type => HASHREF,
 3631:             keys => {
 3632:                 role => {
 3633:                     type => SCALAR,
 3634:                     # Human-readable role description; always defined,
 3635:                     # may contain inline domain/IP/header values.
 3636:                 },
 3637:                 address => {
 3638:                     type  => SCALAR,
 3639:                     regex => qr/^[^\s@]+\@[^\s@]+$/,
 3640:                     # Lower-cased email address; unique across the list.
 3641:                 },
 3642:                 note => {
 3643:                     type => SCALAR,
 3644:                     # Supporting detail; always defined, may be empty string.
 3645:                 },
 3646:                 via => {
 3647:                     type  => SCALAR,
 3648:                     regex => qr/^(?:provider-table|ip-whois|domain-whois)$/,
 3649:                 },
 3650:             },
 3651:         },
 3652:         # ... one hashref per unique address, in first-discovered order
 3653:     )
 3654: 
 3655:     # Empty list when no actionable abuse contacts can be determined.
 3656: 
 3657: =cut
 3658:

 3937: 
 3938: =head2 form_contacts()
 3939: 
 3940: Returns the list of parties that require abuse reports to be submitted via
 3941: a web form rather than (or in addition to) email.  These are providers whose
 3942: C<%PROVIDER_ABUSE> entry has a C<form> key.  Each hashref contains the form
 3943: URL, instructions on what to paste, instructions on what to upload (if
 3944: applicable), the role, and the discovery note.
 3945: 
 3946: Returns a list (not an arrayref) of hashrefs, one per unique form contact,
 3947: in discovery order.  Returns an empty list if no form-only or form-plus-email
 3948: contacts are found.
 3949: 
 3950: Each hashref contains:
 3951: 
 3952: =over 4
 3953: 
 3954: =item C<form> (string) -- the URL of the web form
 3955: 
 3956: =item C<role> (string) -- human-readable role, same format as C<abuse_contacts()>
 3957: 
 3958: =item C<note> (string) -- supporting detail about the provider
 3959: 
 3960: =item C<form_paste> (string, optional) -- what text to paste into the form
 3961: 
 3962: =item C<form_upload> (string, optional) -- what file to attach to the form
 3963: 
 3964: =item C<via> (string) -- always C<'provider-table'>
 3965: 
 3966: =back
 3967: 
 3968: =cut
 3969:

 4117: 
 4118: =head2 report()
 4119: 
 4120: Returns a formatted plain-text abuse report.
 4121: 
 4122: Produces a comprehensive, analyst-facing plain-text report covering all
 4123: findings from every analysis method.  It is the single-document summary
 4124: of everything the module knows about a message: envelope fields, risk
 4125: assessment, originating host, sending software, received chain tracking
 4126: IDs, embedded URLs grouped by hostname, contact domain intelligence, and
 4127: the recommended abuse contacts.
 4128: 
 4129: Use C<report()> when you want a human-readable document for review,
 4130: logging, or a ticketing system.  Use C<abuse_report_text()> when you want
 4131: a compact string to transmit to an ISP abuse desk.
 4132: 
 4133: =head3 Usage
 4134: 
 4135:     $analyser->parse_email($raw);
 4136:     my $text = $analyser->report();
 4137:     print $text;
 4138: 
 4139:     # Write to a file
 4140:     open my $fh, '>', 'report.txt' or die $!;
 4141:     print $fh $analyser->report();
 4142:     close $fh;
 4143: 
 4144:     # Log the risk level line from the report
 4145:     my ($level_line) = $analyser->report() =~ /(\[ RISK ASSESSMENT: [^\]]+\])/;
 4146:     $logger->info($level_line);
 4147: 
 4148:     # Check idempotency -- safe to call multiple times
 4149:     my $r1 = $analyser->report();
 4150:     my $r2 = $analyser->report();
 4151:     # $r1 eq $r2 is always true for the same parsed message
 4152: 
 4153: =head3 Arguments
 4154: 
 4155: None.  C<parse_email()> must have been called first.
 4156: 
 4157: =head3 Returns
 4158: 
 4159: A plain scalar string containing the full report, newline-terminated,
 4160: using Unix line endings (C<\n>) throughout.  The string is never empty;
 4161: it always contains at least the header banner and envelope summary section.
 4162: 
 4163: The report is structured as nine sections separated by blank lines, in
 4164: this fixed order:
 4165: 
 4166: =over 4
 4167: 
 4168: =item 1. Banner
 4169: 
 4170:     ========================================================================
 4171:       Email::Abuse::Investigator Report  (vX.XX)
 4172:     ========================================================================
 4173: 
 4174: A row of 72 equals signs, the module name and version number, and a
 4175: closing row of 72 equals signs.
 4176: 
 4177: =item 2. Envelope summary
 4178: 
 4179: Up to six header fields, each decoded from MIME encoded-words where
 4180: applicable.  If a field was encoded, the decoded form is shown first
 4181: followed by the raw encoded original in brackets:
 4182: 
 4183:     From           : PayPal Security <phish@evil.example>
 4184:     Reply-to       : Replies <harvest@collector.example>
 4185:     Return-path    : <phish@evil.example>
 4186:     Subject        : Account Alert  [encoded: =?UTF-8?B?QWNjb3VudA==?=]
 4187:     Date           : Mon, 01 Jan 2024 00:00:00 +0000
 4188:     Message-id     : <msg001@evil.example>
 4189: 
 4190: Fields examined (in order): C<From:>, C<Reply-To:>, C<Return-Path:>,
 4191: C<Subject:>, C<Date:>, C<Message-ID:>.  Fields not present in the message
 4192: are silently omitted.
 4193: 
 4194: =item 3. Risk assessment
 4195: 
 4196:     [ RISK ASSESSMENT: HIGH (score: 11) ]
 4197:       [HIGH] firmluminary.com was registered 2025-09-01 (less than 180 days ago)
 4198:       [MEDIUM] rDNS 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au looks like a broadband/residential line
 4199:       ...
 4200: 
 4201: Or, when no flags were raised:
 4202: 
 4203:     [ RISK ASSESSMENT: INFO (score: 0) ]
 4204:       (no specific red flags detected)
 4205: 
 4206: Each flag is shown as C<[SEVERITY] detail-string>.
 4207: 
 4208: =item 4. Originating host
 4209: 
 4210:     [ ORIGINATING HOST ]
 4211:       IP           : 120.88.161.249
 4212:       Reverse DNS  : 120-88-161-249.tpgi.com.au
 4213:       Country      : AU
 4214:       Organisation : TPG Telecom Limited
 4215:       Abuse addr   : abuse@tpg.com.au
 4216:       Confidence   : high
 4217:       Note         : First external hop in Received: chain
 4218: 
 4219: Or C<(could not determine originating IP)> if C<originating_ip()> returns
 4220: C<undef>.  Fields with no value are omitted.
 4221: 
 4222: =item 5. Sending software (omitted entirely if no software headers found)
 4223: 
 4224:     [ SENDING SOFTWARE / INFRASTRUCTURE CLUES ]
 4225:       x-php-originating-script : 1000:mailer.php
 4226:       Note           : PHP script on shared hosting -- report to hosting abuse team
 4227: 
 4228: One block per detected header, with its note.
 4229: 
 4230: =item 6. Received chain tracking IDs (omitted if no hops have id or for fields)
 4231: 
 4232:     [ RECEIVED CHAIN TRACKING IDs ]
 4233:       (Supply these to the relevant ISP abuse team to trace the session)
 4234: 
 4235:       IP           : 91.198.174.5
 4236:       Envelope for : victim@bandsman.co.uk
 4237:       Server ID    : ABC123XYZ
 4238: 
 4239: Only hops that have at least one of a session ID (C<id>) or envelope
 4240: recipient (C<for>) are shown; IP-only hops are suppressed.  Oldest hop
 4241: first.
 4242: 
 4243: =item 7. Embedded HTTP/HTTPS URLs
 4244: 
 4245:     [ EMBEDDED HTTP/HTTPS URLs ]
 4246:       Host         : bit.ly  *** URL SHORTENER - real destination hidden ***
 4247:       IP           : 67.199.248.11
 4248:       Country      : US
 4249:       Organisation : Bit.ly LLC
 4250:       Abuse addr   : abuse@bit.ly
 4251:       URL          : https://bit.ly/scam123
 4252: 
 4253: URLs are grouped by hostname; if multiple URLs share a hostname, all
 4254: paths are listed together under the single host block.  Known URL
 4255: shorteners are annotated inline.  Shown as C<(none found)> when the
 4256: body contains no HTTP/HTTPS URLs.
 4257: 
 4258: =item 8. Contact / reply-to domains
 4259: 
 4260:     [ CONTACT / REPLY-TO DOMAINS ]
 4261:       Domain       : firmluminary.com
 4262:       Found in     : From: header
 4263:       *** WARNING: RECENTLY REGISTERED - possible phishing domain ***
 4264:       Registered   : 2025-09-01
 4265:       Expires      : 2026-09-01
 4266:       Registrar    : GoDaddy.com LLC
 4267:       Reg. abuse   : abuse@godaddy.com
 4268:       Web host IP  : 104.21.30.10
 4269:       Web host org : Cloudflare Inc
 4270:       Web abuse    : abuse@cloudflare.com
 4271:       MX host      : mail.firmluminary.com
 4272:       MX IP        : 198.51.100.5
 4273:       MX org       : Hosting Corp
 4274:       MX abuse     : abuse@hostingcorp.example
 4275:       NS host      : ns1.cloudflare.com

 4277:       NS org       : Cloudflare Inc
 4278:       NS abuse     : abuse@cloudflare.com
 4279: 
 4280: One block per domain from C<mailto_domains()>.  Recently-registered
 4281: domains receive an inline warning banner.  Shown as C<(none found)>
 4282: when no qualifying contact domains are present.
 4283: 
 4284: =item 9. Where to send abuse reports
 4285: 
 4286:     [ WHERE TO SEND ABUSE REPORTS ]
 4287:       Role         : Sending ISP
 4288:       Send to      : abuse@tpg.com.au
 4289:       Note         : Network owner of originating IP 120.88.161.249 (TPG Telecom)
 4290:       Discovered   : ip-whois
 4291: 
 4292:       Role         : Domain registrar for firmluminary.com
 4293:       Send to      : abuse@godaddy.com
 4294:       Note         : Registrar: GoDaddy.com LLC
 4295:       Discovered   : domain-whois
 4296: 
 4297: One block per contact from C<abuse_contacts()>.  Shown as
 4298: C<(no abuse contacts could be determined)> when the list is empty.
 4299: 
 4300: =back
 4301: 
 4302: The report ends with a closing row of 72 equals signs.
 4303: 
 4304: =head3 Side Effects
 4305: 
 4306: Calls C<risk_assessment()>, C<originating_ip()>, C<sending_software()>,
 4307: C<received_trail()>, C<embedded_urls()>, C<mailto_domains()>, and
 4308: C<abuse_contacts()> if they have not already run on the current message,
 4309: performing all associated network I/O as documented in those methods.  All
 4310: underlying results are cached; the report text itself is not cached, but
 4311: re-computation is inexpensive since the data is already available.
 4312: 
 4313: =head3 Notes
 4314: 
 4315: =over 4
 4316: 
 4317: =item *
 4318: 
 4319: The report is idempotent: calling C<report()> multiple times on the same
 4320: object always returns an identical string, because all underlying methods
 4321: are cached.
 4322: 
 4323: =item *
 4324: 
 4325: MIME encoded-words in the C<From:>, C<Subject:>, and other displayed
 4326: headers are decoded for readability.  When a header was encoded, both the
 4327: decoded form and the raw encoded original are shown, so the report is
 4328: useful both for human reading and for log parsing.
 4329: 
 4330: =item *
 4331: 
 4332: URL hosts in section 7 are grouped by hostname and shown in first-seen
 4333: order.  Multiple URLs on the same host are listed together rather than
 4334: repeating the host's IP and WHOIS information, keeping the output compact
 4335: even when a message contains dozens of tracking-pixel and click-redirect
 4336: URLs all on the same CDN.
 4337: 
 4338: =item *
 4339: 
 4340: The received-trail section (section 6) filters out hops that have only an
 4341: IP address and no C<id> or C<for> clause.  The full unfiltered trail is
 4342: available via C<received_trail()>.
 4343: 
 4344: =item *
 4345: 
 4346: Section 5 (sending software) and section 6 (received chain tracking IDs)
 4347: are entirely omitted -- no heading, no placeholder text -- when no relevant
 4348: headers are present.  All other sections always appear, using a
 4349: C<(none found)> or equivalent placeholder when their data is empty.
 4350: 
 4351: =item *
 4352: 
 4353: The version number in the banner is the value of C<$Email::Abuse::Investigator::VERSION>
 4354: at the time C<report()> is called.
 4355: 
 4356: =back
 4357: 
 4358: =head3 API Specification
 4359: 
 4360: =head4 Input
 4361: 
 4362:     # Params::Validate::Strict compatible specification
 4363:     # No arguments.
 4364:     []
 4365: 
 4366: =head4 Output
 4367: 
 4368:     # Return::Set compatible specification
 4369:     {
 4370:         type  => SCALAR,
 4371:         # Non-empty plain-text string, newline-terminated (\n).
 4372:         # Always defined; never undef.
 4373:         # Line endings: Unix LF (\n) only.
 4374:         # Structure: nine fixed sections in the order documented above,
 4375:         #            separated by blank lines, framed by 72-character
 4376:         #            equals-sign banners.
 4377:     }
 4378: 
 4379: =cut
 4380:

 4595: 
 4596: # _split_message( $text )
 4597: #
 4598: # Entry criteria:
 4599: #   $text  -- a defined scalar containing a raw RFC 2822 email message,
 4600: #             with headers and body separated by a blank line (\n\n or
 4601: #             \r\n\r\n).  Both LF and CRLF line endings are accepted.
 4602: #             The text must already be dereferenced (parse_email() handles
 4603: #             the scalar-ref case before calling this method).
 4604: #             Called only from parse_email(); $self->{_sending_sw} and
 4605: #             $self->{_rcvd_tracking} must have been reset to [] by the
 4606: #             caller before this method is invoked.
 4607: #
 4608: # Exit status:
 4609: #   Returns undef (and does nothing further) if $header_block is undef or
 4610: #   contains only whitespace -- i.e. the message has no headers or is
 4611: #   empty.  Otherwise returns no meaningful value; all results are
 4612: #   communicated through side effects on $self.
 4613: #
 4614: # Side effects:
 4615: #   $self->{_headers}      set to an arrayref of { name => lc, value => raw }
 4616: #                          hashrefs, one per parsed header, in message order.
 4617: #                          Folded (multi-line) values are unfolded before
 4618: #                          parsing (RFC 2822 s2.2.3).  Header names are
 4619: #                          normalised to lower-case.
 4620: #   $self->{_received}     set to an arrayref of raw Received: header values
 4621: #                          (not decoded), in message order (most-recent first).
 4622: #   $self->{_body_plain}   set to the decoded plain-text body.  Appended to
 4623: #                          (not replaced) for each text/* part in multipart
 4624: #                          messages.
 4625: #   $self->{_body_html}    set to the decoded HTML body.  Appended to for
 4626: #                          each text/html part in multipart messages.
 4627: #   $self->{_sending_sw}   populated with { header, value, note } hashrefs
 4628: #                          for any of the six recognised software-fingerprint
 4629: #                          headers that are present, in alphabetical key order.
 4630: #   $self->{_rcvd_tracking} populated with { received, ip, for, id } hashrefs,
 4631: #                          one per Received: hop from which at least one of
 4632: #                          an IP, envelope recipient, or session ID could be
 4633: #                          extracted, in oldest-first order.
 4634: #
 4635: # Notes:
 4636: #   Delegates body decoding to _decode_multipart() for multipart/* content
 4637: #   types (which recursively handles each part) or to _decode_body() for
 4638: #   single-part messages.  If Content-Type is absent or unrecognised, the
 4639: #   body is treated as plain text with 7bit encoding.
 4640: #   The boundary parameter in multipart Content-Type is extracted with a
 4641: #   simple regex; missing or malformed boundaries cause the body to be
 4642: #   silently skipped.
 4643: #   Lines that do not match the header pattern /^([\w-]+)\s*:\s*(.*)/ are
 4644: #   silently discarded (covers blank lines and non-header preamble text).
 4645: 
 4646: sub _split_message {
●4647 → 4658 → 4663●4647 → 4658 → 0 4647:     my ($self, $text) = @_;
 4648:

 4781: 
 4782: # _find_origin()
 4783: #
 4784: #   Identifies the IP address of the machine that originally injected the
 4785: #   message into the public mail system by walking the Received: chain and
 4786: #   discarding every hop that belongs to private, reserved, or
 4787: #   caller-trusted infrastructure.  The first remaining (oldest external)
 4788: #   IP is enriched with reverse DNS, organisation, abuse contact, and
 4789: #   country information and returned as the origin hashref.
 4790: #
 4791: #   This is the back-end implementation for the public originating_ip()
 4792: #   method, which caches the result.  _find_origin() itself performs no
 4793: #   caching and must not be called directly; always call originating_ip().
 4794: #
 4795: # Entry criteria:
 4796: #   No arguments beyond $self.
 4797: #   $self->{_received}     must be populated (by _split_message()).
 4798: #   $self->{_headers}      must be populated (by _split_message()), so
 4799: #                          that _header_value('x-originating-ip') works.
 4800: #   $self->{trusted_relays} must be an arrayref (set by new(); may be []).
 4801: #
 4802: # Exit status:
 4803: #   Returns a hashref on success -- the same structure as originating_ip():
 4804: #     { ip, rdns, org, abuse, country, confidence, note }
 4805: #   Returns undef if no usable originating IP can be determined:
 4806: #     -- all Received: IPs are private, reserved, or trusted; AND
 4807: #     -- X-Originating-IP is absent, private, or unparseable.
 4808: #
 4809: # Side effects:
 4810: #   Performs network I/O via _enrich_ip():
 4811: #     - one PTR (rDNS) lookup for the chosen IP (_reverse_dns)
 4812: #     - one RDAP or WHOIS query for the chosen IP (_whois_ip)
 4813: #   No state is written to $self; the result is returned, not cached here.
 4814: #
 4815: # Notes:
 4816: #   The Received: chain is walked in reverse message order -- i.e. from
 4817: #   the oldest header (bottom of the header block) to the most recent --
 4818: #   so that candidates are accumulated in oldest-first order.  $candidates[0]
 4819: #   is always the outermost (first) external relay.
 4820: #
 4821: #   Confidence levels are assigned as follows:
 4822: #     'high'   -- two or more distinct external IPs found in the chain.
 4823: #                 Multiple independent relay records corroborate the origin.
 4824: #     'medium' -- exactly one external IP found in the chain.
 4825: #     'low'    -- no usable Received: IP; origin taken from
 4826: #                 X-Originating-IP, which is injected by webmail providers
 4827: #                 and is not independently verifiable.  Brackets and
 4828: #                 whitespace are stripped from the header value before use.
 4829: #
 4830: #   _is_private() treats undef and the empty string as private, so a
 4831: #   Received: header from which no IP can be extracted is silently skipped
 4832: #   without special-casing.
 4833: #
 4834: #   IPv6 addresses are not extracted by _extract_ip_from_received(); only
 4835: #   dotted-quad IPv4 addresses are considered.
 4836:
